<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Net flows for 2006 were $15.3&nbsp;billion, up 13% from the prior year&#146;s level. Net flows into
closed-end funds were down $1.7&nbsp;billion when compared to the prior year due to fewer new offerings
in 2006. Mutual fund net flows were up $1.8&nbsp;billion when compared to the prior year due to
increased sales. Retail managed account net flows were down $1.1&nbsp;billion behind the closing (to
new investors) in 2006 of our Tradewinds international value style strategy. Institutional managed
account flows increased $2.8&nbsp;billion for the year when compared to the prior year. The main driver
of this growth was an increase in Tradewinds&#146; value-style international managed account flows.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Net flows for 2005 totaled $13.6&nbsp;billion, down 10% from the prior year&#146;s record level. Managed
account flows were particularly strong, with our value-style equity accounts contributing $9.9
billion in flows and our municipal-style account flows adding another $1.4&nbsp;billion. Partially
offsetting the positive flows were $3.2&nbsp;billion in growth-style equity account outflows. Mutual
funds flows in 2005 were more than six times flows in 2004, driven by both municipal and equity
flows.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Net flows in 2006 of $15.3&nbsp;billion coupled with $10.2&nbsp;billion of market appreciation
resulted in a 19% increase in assets under management in 2006. Closed-end fund assets grew $1.0
billion, driven by $0.6&nbsp;billion in net flows and $0.4&nbsp;billion in market appreciation. Mutual fund
assets grew $4&nbsp;billion driven by $3.6&nbsp;billion in net flows and $0.4&nbsp;billion in market appreciation.
Managed account assets increased $20.5&nbsp;billion driven by $11.1&nbsp;billion in new flows and $9.4
billion in market appreciation.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">When comparing 2005 with 2004, assets under management increased $20.7&nbsp;billion, or 18%, to over
$136&nbsp;billion. Strong flows, the acquisition of Santa Barbara, and market appreciation were key
contributors. Closed-end fund assets grew $1.8&nbsp;billion, driven
by $2.4&nbsp;billion in net flows, offset by $0.6&nbsp;billion in fixed-income market depreciation. Mutual fund assets grew $1.8
billion driven entirely by new flows. Managed account assets increased $17.1&nbsp;billion due to $9.4
billion in net flows and $4.3&nbsp;billion in equity market appreciation. The acquisition of Santa
Barbara added $3.4&nbsp;billion to managed assets.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Higher asset levels in 2006 contributed to a 23% increase in advisory fees in 2006. Advisory fees
on mutual funds increased 27%, while managed account fees increased 43%. Within the managed
account product line, advisory fee revenue increased on both value-style equity and municipal-style
accounts, while declining on growth-style equity accounts, excluding the impact of the Santa
Barbara acquisition. Advisory fees on closed-end funds increased 1% for the year.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Advisory fees increased 18% during 2005, driven mainly by higher asset levels for both closed-end
funds and managed accounts. Advisory fees on closed-end funds increased 4%, while managed account
fees increased 38%.
</DIV>

        <TD nowrap colspan="2" align="right" style="border-top: 3px double #000000">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
        <TD nowrap colspan="2" align="right" style="border-top: 3px double #000000">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
</TR>
<!-- End Table Body -->
</TABLE>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Product distribution revenue declined in 2006 when compared with the prior year. Underwriting
revenue on closed-end funds declined $2.1&nbsp;million due to fewer new fund assets raised in 2006.
Mutual fund distribution revenue declined $1.0&nbsp;million, despite an increase in mutual fund sales,
as a result of an increase in commissions paid on large dollar value sales. Muni Preferred<SUP style="font-size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">&#174;</SUP> and
Fund Preferred<SUP style="font-size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">&#174;</SUP> fees also declined slightly for the year. This decline is due to a decline in
shares traded by non-participating brokers who access the auction through the Company&#146;s trading
desk.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Product distribution revenue declined slightly in 2005 when compared with the prior year as a
decline in underwriting revenue on closed-end funds and mutual fund distribution revenue was offset
by an increase in Muni Preferred<SUP style="font-size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">&#174;</SUP> and Fund Preferred<SUP style="font-size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">&#174;</SUP> fees.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B><I>Performance Fees/Other Revenue</I></B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Performance fees/other revenue consists of performance fees earned on institutional assets managed
and various fees earned in connection with services provided on behalf of our defined portfolio
assets under surveillance.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Performance fees for 2006 were $18.5&nbsp;million, down from $19.8&nbsp;million in 2005. In
addition, fees earned on services provided on behalf of our defined portfolio assets under
surveillance declined due to an overall decline in these assets.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Performance fees in 2005 were $1.7&nbsp;million higher than in 2004.
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->25<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Summary</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Operating expenses increased $90&nbsp;million or 30% in 2006 and $46.5&nbsp;million or 18% in 2005, driven
mainly by increases in compensation and benefits as we continue to invest in the further growth and
development of our business. As a result of this targeted investment, we saw expenses as a percent
of revenue increase from 50.8% to 54.8% in 2006.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><B>Compensation and Benefits</B><BR>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Compensation and related benefits for 2006 increased $68.5&nbsp;million. This increase was the result of
increases in base compensation as a result of new positions and salary increases, as well as
increases in overall incentive compensation due to the Company&#146;s higher profit level. A portion of
the increase in overall incentive compensation related to expense recognized in connection with
various equity-based profits interests awarded to affiliates. The fair market value of unvested
profits interests is being expensed over the appropriate vesting period of the related units as a
compensation charge, with a corresponding increase in minority interest outstanding (see also
&#147;Capital Resources, Liquidity and Financial Condition&#148; section below for further information). In
addition, during 2006, management determined that it appeared probable the Company will meet the
performance requirements as set forth in a long-term equity performance plan (&#147;LTEP&#148;). As a
result, during 2006, the Company expensed a total of $8.7&nbsp;million related to the LTEP awards, which
included $4.2&nbsp;million of a &#147;catch-up&#148; adjustment for amortization as if the plan had been expensed
for prior periods from the date of the LTEP grant (January&nbsp;2005) through January&nbsp;2006.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Compensation and related benefits for 2005 increased $29.9&nbsp;million with approximately 50% of the
increase attributable to higher annual incentive compensation which is tied to Company
profitability. The remaining increase was due to annual salary increases and higher health care
expenses as well as the cost of increased staffing levels, as we invested in virtually all aspects
of our operations.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><B>Advertising and Promotional Costs</B><BR>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Advertising and promotional expenditures increased $1.0&nbsp;million in 2006 and $0.3&nbsp;million in 2005
due to expanded product launches in both years.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><B>Amortization of Intangible Assets</B><BR>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Amortization of intangible assets increased $2.9&nbsp;million during 2006 and $0.4&nbsp;million during 2005
as a result of amortization of intangible assets associated with the Santa Barbara acquisition.
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->26<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><B>Outside and Professional Services</B><BR>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Outside and professional services increased $5.8&nbsp;million during 2006 due mainly to an increase in
electronic information expense as we provide our investment and research teams with more data and
other tools to better manage their portfolios.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Outside and professional services increased $2.8&nbsp;million during 2005 due mainly to an increase in
electronic information expenses.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><B>Minority Interest Expense</B><BR>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Minority interest expense results from key employees at NWQ, Tradewinds, Symphony, and Santa
Barbara having been granted non-controlling equity-based profits interests in their respective
businesses. For additional information on minority interest expense, please refer to the &#147;Capital
Resources, Liquidity and Financial Condition&#148; section.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><B>All Other Operating Expenses</B><BR>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">All other operating expenses increased $10.9&nbsp;million during 2006. Approximately $2.0&nbsp;million of
the increase is due to an increase in structuring fees and fund organization costs paid on the
initial offering of our closed-end funds. Occupancy and equipment costs increased $2.5&nbsp;million as
a result of an increase in leased space. Travel and entertainment spending increased $1.8&nbsp;million
as a result of our 2006 product launches. The remainder of the increase relates to higher
insurance costs and higher bank facility costs related to our bank line of credit.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">All other operating expenses increased $9.2&nbsp;million during 2005. Approximately $3.3&nbsp;million of the
increase is due to structuring fees paid on the initial offering of two closed-end funds.
Occupancy and equipment costs increased $1.9&nbsp;million as a result of an increase in leased space for
NWQ, Tradewinds and Santa Barbara. The remainder of the increase relates to higher insurance costs
and higher bank facility costs related to our bank line of credit.
</DIV>

which was acquired by New York Life Investment Management. During 2006, the Company recorded a
gain of $10.1&nbsp;million on the sale. In addition to the ICAP gain, the Company recognized
approximately $5&nbsp;million in gains on the sale of seed investments in new products and portfolios.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Total other income/(expense) was $7.9&nbsp;million in 2005. As a result of the early repayment of the
Company&#146;s previously outstanding $300&nbsp;million of private placement debt, the Company accelerated
the recognition of
</DIV>

of miscellaneous income for the year. Supplementing this other income was $4.8&nbsp;million in gains

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><U><B>Recent Accounting Pronouncements</B></U>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>FIN 48</I>

</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On July&nbsp;13, 2006, the Financial Accounting Standards Board (&#147;FASB&#148;) issued the final Interpretation
No.&nbsp;48, &#147;Accounting for Uncertainty in Income Taxes&#148; (&#147;FIN 48&#148;). FIN 48 is effective for us as of
January&nbsp;1, 2007, and supplements SFAS No.&nbsp;109, &#147;Accounting for Income Taxes,&#148; by defining the
confidence level that a tax position must meet in order to be recognized in the financial
statements. FIN 48 requires that the tax effects of a position be recognized only if it is
&#147;more-likely-than-not&#148; to be sustained based solely on its technical merits as of the reporting
date. The term &#147;more-likely-than-not&#148; means a likelihood of more than fifty percent. In addition,
FIN 48 requires new annual disclosures in the notes to the financial statements. Tabular
disclosure of the beginning and ending balances of unrecognized tax benefits, as well as
significant increases and/or decreases to unrecognized tax benefits, is required. The Company does not expect FIN 48 to have a material impact to its financial statements.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>SFAS No.&nbsp;157</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On September&nbsp;15, 2006, the FASB issued SFAS No.&nbsp;157, &#147;Fair Value Measurements,&#148; (&#147;SFAS No.&nbsp;157&#148;).
SFAS No.&nbsp;157 provides enhanced guidance for using fair value to measure assets and liabilities by
defining fair value, establishing a framework for measuring fair value, and expanding disclosure
requirements about fair value measurements. SFAS No.&nbsp;157 does not require any new fair value
measurements. Prior to this standard, methods for measuring fair value were diverse and
inconsistent, especially for items that are not actively traded. The standard clarifies that, for
items that are not actively traded, such as certain kinds of derivatives, that fair value should
reflect the price in a transaction with a market participant, including an adjustment for risk, not
just a company&#146;s mark-to-market model value. The standard also requires expanded disclosure of the
effect on earnings for items measured using unobservable data.
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->28<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Under SFAS No.&nbsp;157, fair value refers to the price that would be received to sell an asset or paid
to transfer a liability in an orderly transaction between market participants in the market in
which the reporting entity transacts. SFAS No.&nbsp;157 clarifies the principle that fair value should
be based on the assumptions market participants would use when pricing the asset or liability. In
support of this principle, SFAS No.&nbsp;157 establishes a fair value hierarchy that prioritizes the
information used to develop those assumptions. The fair value hierarchy gives the highest priority
to quoted prices in active markets and the lowest priority to unobservable data (for example, the
reporting entity&#146;s own data). Finally, under SFAS No.&nbsp;157, fair value measurements would be
separately disclosed by level within the fair value hierarchy.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">SFAS No.&nbsp;157 is effective for financial statements issued for fiscal years beginning after November
15, 2007, and interim periods within those fiscal years. Early adoption is permitted. The Company
has not completed a study of what effect SFAS No.&nbsp;157 will have on its financial position and
results of operations.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><U><B>Capital Resources, Liquidity and Financial Condition</B></U>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Our primary liquidity needs are to fund capital expenditures, service indebtedness and support
working capital requirements. Our principal sources of liquidity are cash flows from operating
activities and borrowings under available credit facilities and long-term notes.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><B><I>Private Placement Debt</I></B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On September&nbsp;19, 2003, the Company issued $300&nbsp;million of senior unsecured notes (the &#147;private
placement debt&#148;). Proceeds from the private placement debt were used to refinance existing debt
and for general corporate purposes. These notes, which carried a fixed coupon rate of 4.22%,
payable semi-annually, were issued at 100% of par, were unsecured and were prepayable at any time
in whole or in part. These notes were originally scheduled to mature on September&nbsp;19, 2008, but
were repaid on April&nbsp;6, 2005, with borrowings made under a bridge credit agreement (discussed
below). At the time of the repayment, the Company also paid approximately $1.5&nbsp;million in accrued
interest. Under the terms of the private placement debt, no &#147;make-whole premium&#148; amounts were due.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><B><I>Bank Credit Facilities</I></B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Since 2003, the Company maintained a line of credit with a group of banks. This $250&nbsp;million
credit line was divided into two equal facilities: one with a three-year term that was scheduled
to expire in August of 2006, and one with a term of 364&nbsp;days that was scheduled to expire in August
2005. During the second quarter of 2005, the Company terminated the 364-day line of credit, and
amended the three-year line of credit to permit the borrowings under a bridge financing
agreement and the use of those borrowings as described below. During the third quarter of 2005,
the Company terminated the three-year term facility and replaced it with a new senior revolving
credit facility (discussed below).
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><B><I>Bridge Credit Facility</I></B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In April&nbsp;2005, the Company entered into a $750&nbsp;million bridge credit agreement with various
financial institutions. The original maturity date of this credit agreement was March&nbsp;31, 2006.
Borrowings under this facility bore an interest rate, at Nuveen Investments&#146; option, of either
LIBOR or the Federal Funds rate plus a spread equal to 0.335% to 0.470% based on Nuveen
Investments&#146; leverage, with such applicable spread increasing by 0.25% on September&nbsp;30, 2005, and
by an additional 0.25% on December&nbsp;31, 2005. The bridge credit agreement required Nuveen
Investments to pay a facility fee quarterly in arrears in an annual amount ranging from 0.09% to
0.13%, depending on Nuveen Investments&#146; leverage ratio, and, when applicable, a utilization fee.
During the second quarter of 2005, the Company used approximately $300&nbsp;million of the amount
available under the facility to prepay the holders of the Company&#146;s 4.22% senior unsecured notes
due September&nbsp;19, 2008. During the third quarter of 2005, the Company used an additional $410
million of the remaining amount available under the bridge credit agreement primarily to fulfill
its forward contract obligation to repurchase shares of its common stock owned by STA (refer to
Note 1 to the Consolidated
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->29<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Financial Statements &#147;Sale of The St. Paul Travelers Companies, Inc.&#146;s Ownership Interest in Nuveen Investments&#148;). During the third quarter of 2005, the entire $710
million borrowed under the bridge credit agreement was repaid with borrowings made under a
senior revolving credit facility and the issuance of senior notes (both discussed below) and the
bridge credit facility was terminated.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><B><I>Senior Term Notes</I></B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On September&nbsp;12, 2005, Nuveen Investments issued $550&nbsp;million of senior unsecured notes, consisting
of $250&nbsp;million of 5-year notes and $300&nbsp;million of 10-year notes. The Company received
approximately $544.4&nbsp;million in net proceeds after discounts and underwriting commissions. The
5-year notes bear interest at an annual fixed rate of 5.0%, payable semi-annually beginning March
15, 2006. The 10-year senior notes bear interest at an annual fixed rate of 5.5%, payable
semi-annually also beginning March&nbsp;15, 2006. The net proceeds from the notes were used to repay a
portion of the outstanding debt under the bridge credit facility. The costs related to the
issuance of the senior term notes were capitalized and are being amortized to expense over their
respective terms.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><B><I>Senior Revolving Credit Facility</I></B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In addition to the senior term notes, the Company has a $400&nbsp;million senior revolving credit
facility entered into in September&nbsp;2005 that expires on September&nbsp;15, 2010. As of December&nbsp;31,
2005, the Company borrowed $150&nbsp;million of the total amount available under the senior revolving
credit facility. The proceeds under this borrowing were used to repay the remaining amount due
under the bridge credit facility. During the second quarter of 2006, the Company repaid $50
million under this credit facility, and as of December&nbsp;31, 2006, the Company had $100&nbsp;million
outstanding under this facility. The rate of interest payable under the agreement is, at the
Company&#146;s option, a function of either one of various floating rate indices or the Federal Funds
rate. The agreement requires the Company to pay a facility fee at an annual rate of a range of
0.08% to 0.15% that is dependent on our debt rating. Proceeds from borrowings under this facility
may be used for fulfilling day-to-day cash requirements and general corporate purposes, including
acquisitions, share repurchases and asset purchases. There are conventional financial covenants
associated with this credit facility, including a minimum net worth requirement and a maximum
leverage ratio. We were in compliance with those covenants as of December&nbsp;31, 2006.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><B><I>Other</I></B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In addition to the above facilities, our broker-dealer subsidiary may utilize available,
uncommitted lines of credit with no annual facility fees, which approximate $50&nbsp;million, to satisfy
periodic, unanticipated, short-term liquidity needs. As of December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005, no
borrowings were outstanding on these uncommitted lines of credit.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><B><I>Adequacy of Liquidity</I></B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Management believes that cash provided from operations and borrowings available under its
uncommitted and committed credit facilities will provide the Company with sufficient liquidity to
meet its working capital needs, planned capital expenditures, future contractual obligations and
payment of its anticipated quarterly dividends.

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><B><I>Equity and Dividends</I></B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">As part of the NWQ acquisition, key management purchased a non-controlling, member interest in NWQ
Investment Management Company, LLC. The non-controlling interest of $0.3&nbsp;million as of December
31, 2006, and $0.4&nbsp;million as of December&nbsp;31, 2005, is reflected in minority interest on the
consolidated balance sheets. This purchase allows management to participate in profits of NWQ
above specified levels beginning January&nbsp;1, 2003. During 2006 and 2005, we recorded approximately
$3.8&nbsp;million and $5.6&nbsp;million, respectively, of minority interest expense, which reflects the
portion of profits applicable to the minority owners. Beginning in 2004 and continuing through
2008, the Company has the right to purchase the non-controlling members&#146; respective interests in
NWQ at fair value. On February&nbsp;13, 2004, the Company exercised its right to call 100% of the Class
2 minority members&#146; interests for $15.4&nbsp;million. Of the total amount paid, approximately $12.9
million was recorded as goodwill. On February&nbsp;15, 2005, the Company exercised its right to call
100% of the Class&nbsp;3 NWQ minority members&#146; interests for
$22.8&nbsp;million. Of the total amount paid,
approximately $22.5&nbsp;million was recorded as goodwill. On February&nbsp;15, 2006, the Company exercised
its right to call 25% of the Class&nbsp;4 NWQ minority members&#146; interests for $22.6&nbsp;million. Of the
total amount paid on March&nbsp;1, 2006, approximately $22.5&nbsp;million was recorded as goodwill.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">As part of the Santa Barbara acquisition, an equity opportunity was put in place to allow key
individuals to participate in Santa Barbara&#146;s earnings growth over the next five years (Class&nbsp;2
Units, Class&nbsp;5A Units, Class&nbsp;5B Units, and Class&nbsp;6 Units, collectively referred to as &#147;Units&#148;).
The Class&nbsp;2 Units were fully vested upon issuance. The Class&nbsp;5A Units shall vest one third on June
30, 2007, one third on June&nbsp;30, 2008, and one third on June&nbsp;30, 2009. One third of the Class&nbsp;5B
Units vested upon issuance, one third on June&nbsp;30, 2007, and one

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">third on June&nbsp;30, 2009. The Class&nbsp;6 Units shall vest on June&nbsp;30, 2009. During 2006, we recorded
approximately $1.2&nbsp;million of minority interest expense, which reflects the portion of profits
applicable to the minority owners. The Units entitle the holders to receive a distribution of the
cash flow from Santa Barbara&#146;s business to the extent such cash flow exceeds certain thresholds.
The distribution thresholds vary from year to year, reflecting Santa Barbara achieving certain
profit levels and the distributions of profits interests are also subject to a cap in each year.
Beginning in 2008 and continuing through 2012, the Company has the right to acquire the Units of
the non-controlling members.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">During 2006, new equity opportunities were put in place covering NWQ, Tradewinds and Symphony.
These programs allow key individuals of these businesses to participate in the growth of their
respective businesses over the next five years. Classes of units were established at each
subsidiary (collectively referred to as &#147;Units&#148;). Certain of these Units vest on June&nbsp;30 of 2007,
2008, 2009, 2010 and 2011. During 2006, we recorded approximately $1.2&nbsp;million of minority
interest expense, which reflects the portion of profits applicable to minority owners. The Units
entitle the holders to receive a distribution of the cash flow from their business to the extent
such cash flow exceeds certain thresholds. The distribution thresholds increase from year to year
and the distributions of the profits interests are also subject to a cap in each year. Beginning
in 2008 and continuing through 2012, the Company has the right to acquire the Units of the
non-controlling members.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">At December&nbsp;31, 2006, we held in treasury 42,096,405 shares of the Company&#146;s common stock. During
2006, the Company repurchased 1,963,497 common stock shares in open market transactions as part of
an on-going repurchase program. As part of a share repurchase program approved on August&nbsp;9, 2006,
we are authorized to purchase up to 7.0&nbsp;million shares of common stock. As of December&nbsp;31, 2006,
the remaining authorization covered 6.6&nbsp;million shares.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">During 2006, we paid out dividends on common shares totaling $73.1&nbsp;million. See Note 15 to the
Consolidated Financial Statements, &#147;Quarterly Results (Unaudited),&#148; for a summary of our dividends
paid during the last two fiscal years.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><B><I>Broker-Dealer</I></B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Our broker-dealer subsidiary is subject to requirements of the Securities and Exchange Commission
relating to liquidity and capital standards (See Note 14 to the Consolidated Financial Statements
&#147;Net Capital Requirement&#148;).
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><U><B>Critical Accounting Policies</B></U>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Our financial statements and accompanying notes are prepared in accordance with accounting
principles generally accepted in the United States of America. Preparing financial statements
requires management to make estimates and assumptions that impact our financial position and
results of operations. These estimates and assumptions are affected by our application of
accounting policies. Below we describe certain critical accounting policies that we believe are
important to the understanding of our results of operations and financial position. In addition,
please refer to Note 1 to the Consolidated Financial Statements for further discussion of our
accounting policies.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><B><I>Intangible Assets</I></B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">At December&nbsp;31, 2006, our assets included $634&nbsp;million of goodwill and $67&nbsp;million of other
definite-lived intangible assets. Under Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No.&nbsp;142,
&#147;Goodwill and Other Intangible Assets,&#148; we are required to test the fair value of goodwill and
indefinite-lived intangibles on an annual basis and between annual tests in certain circumstances.
Application of the goodwill impairment test requires judgment, including the identification of
reporting units, assigning assets and liabilities to reporting units, assigning goodwill to
reporting units and determining the fair value of each reporting unit. Significant judgments
required to estimate the fair value of reporting units include estimating future cash flows,
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->32<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">



<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">determining appropriate market multiples and other assumptions. We completed the impairment
testing of goodwill and determined that there was no impairment to the goodwill recorded in our
books and records as of May&nbsp;31, 2006, the date that we have selected as an annual date. The
recognition of any such impairment would have resulted in a charge to income in the period in which
the impairment was determined. While we believe that our testing was appropriate, the use of
different assumptions may result in recognizing some impairment of goodwill in our financial
statements.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B><I>Impairment of Investment Securities</I></B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">SFAS No.&nbsp;115, &#147;Accounting for Certain Investments in Debt and Equity Securities&#148; and Securities and
Exchange Commission (&#147;SEC&#148;) Staff Accounting Bulletin (&#147;SAB&#148;) 59, &#147;Accounting for Noncurrent
Marketable Equity Securities&#148; and FASB Emerging Issues Task Force (&#147;EITF&#148;) 03-01, &#147;The Meaning of
Other-Than-Temporary Impairment and Its Application to Certain Investments&#148; provide guidance on
determining when an investment is other-than-temporarily impaired. We periodically evaluate our
investments for other-than-temporary declines in value. To determine if an other-than-temporary
decline exists, we evaluate, among other factors, general market conditions, the duration and
extent to which the fair value is less than cost, as well as our intent and ability to hold the
investment. Additionally, we consider the financial health of and near-term business outlook for a
counterparty, including factors such as industry performance and operational cash flow. If an
other-than-temporary decline in value is determined to exist, the unrealized investment loss net of
tax, in accumulated other comprehensive income, is realized as a charge to net income in that
period. See Note 1 to the Consolidated Financial Statements for further information.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B><I>Accounting for Income Taxes</I></B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">SFAS No.&nbsp;109, &#147;Accounting for Income Taxes,&#148; establishes financial accounting and reporting
standards for the effect of income taxes. The objectives of accounting for income taxes are to
recognize the amount of taxes payable or refundable for the current year and deferred tax
liabilities and assets for the future tax consequences of events that have been recognized in an
entity&#146;s financial statements or tax returns. Judgment is required in assessing the future tax
consequences of events that have been recognized in our financial statements or tax returns.
Fluctuations in the actual outcome of these future tax consequences could impact our financial
position or our results of operations.
</DIV>

cause our assets under management, earnings, revenues, profit margins, and/or our stock price to
decline include: (1)&nbsp;the effects of the substantial competition that we, like all market
participants, face in the investment management business; (2)&nbsp;our inability to access third-party
distribution channels to market our products or a related

<!-- link2 "Item&nbsp;7a. Quantitative and Qualitative Disclosures About Market Risk" -->
<DIV align="left"><A NAME="011"></A></DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Item&nbsp;7a. Quantitative and Qualitative Disclosures About Market Risk</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><B><I>Market Risk</I></B>

</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The
following information, and information included elsewhere in this report, describe the key
aspects of certain financial instruments that have market risk.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Interest Rate Sensitivity</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">As of
December&nbsp;31, 2006 and December&nbsp;31, 2005, we had
$100&nbsp;million and $150&nbsp;million, respectively, outstanding under our senior revolving credit
facility. The rate of interest payable under the agreement is, at the Company&#146;s option, a function
of either one of various floating rate indices or the Federal Funds rate. We estimate that a 100
basis point increase (1&nbsp;percentage point) in interest rates from
the level at December&nbsp;31, 2006 and December&nbsp;31, 2005,
would result in a $1.0&nbsp;million and $1.5&nbsp;million increase,
respectively, in annual interest expense; however, it would have no
impact on the fair value of the debt at December&nbsp;31, 2006 or
December&nbsp;31, 2005. In addition to the debt
outstanding under our revolving credit facility at December&nbsp;31,
2006 and December&nbsp;31, 2005, we also had $550&nbsp;million of
senior unsecured notes, including $250&nbsp;million of 5-year notes and $300&nbsp;million of 10-year notes.
The 5-year notes will bear interest at an annual fixed rate of 5.0% payable semi-annually,
beginning March&nbsp;15, 2006. The 10-year senior notes will bear interest at an annual fixed rate of
5.5% payable semi-annually, also beginning March&nbsp;15, 2006. A change in interest rates would have
had no impact on interest incurred on our fixed rate debt or cash flow, but would have had an
impact on the fair value of the debt. We estimate that a 100 basis point increase in interest
rates from the levels at December&nbsp;31, 2006, and
December&nbsp;31, 2005, would have resulted in a net decrease in the fair value
of our debt of approximately $27&nbsp;million at December&nbsp;31,
2006 and $31&nbsp;million at December&nbsp;31, 2005.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Our investments consist primarily of Company-sponsored managed investment funds that invest in a
variety of asset classes. Additionally, the Company periodically invests in new advisory accounts
to establish a performance history prior to a potential product launch. Company-sponsored funds
and accounts are carried on our consolidated financial statements at fair market value and are
subject to the investment performance of the underlying sponsored fund or account. Any unrealized
gain or loss is recognized upon the sale of the investment. The carrying value of the Company&#146;s
investments in fixed-income funds or accounts, which expose us to interest rate risk, was
approximately $63&nbsp;million and $45&nbsp;million at December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005, respectively. We estimate
that a 100 basis point increase in interest rates from the levels at December&nbsp;31, 2006, would
result in a net decrease of approximately $1.8&nbsp;million in the fair value of the fixed-income
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->34<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">



<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">investments at December&nbsp;31, 2006. We estimate that a 100 basis point increase in interest rates
from the levels at December&nbsp;31, 2005, would have resulted in a net decrease of approximately $1.7
million in the fair value of the fixed-income investments at December&nbsp;31, 2005.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Also included in investments at December&nbsp;31, 2006, are certain swap agreements and futures
contracts that are sensitive to changes in interest rates. The futures contracts and swap
agreements are being used to mitigate overall market risk related to our investments in recently
created product portfolios that are not yet marketed. The fair value of these instruments totaled
approximately $0.3&nbsp;million at December&nbsp;31, 2006, and December&nbsp;31, 2005. We estimate that a 100
basis point increase in interest rates from the levels at December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005, would have
resulted in a net increase in the fair market value of the open derivatives of $1.7&nbsp;million. See
Note 5 &#147;Derivative Financial Instruments&#148; to our Consolidated Financial Statements for more
information.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Equity Market Sensitivity</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">As discussed above in the interest rate sensitivity section, we invest in certain Company-sponsored
managed investment funds and accounts that invest in a variety of asset classes. The carrying
value of the Company&#146;s investments in funds and accounts subject to equity price risk is
approximately $55&nbsp;million and $45&nbsp;million, at December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005, respectively. As of
December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005, we estimate that a 10% adverse change in equity prices would have
resulted in decreases of approximately $5&nbsp;million in the fair value of our equity securities. The
model to determine sensitivity assumes a corresponding shift in all equity prices.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">An adverse movement in the equity price of our holdings in privately-held companies cannot be
easily quantified as our ability to realize returns on our investment depends on the investees&#146;
ability to raise additional capital and/or derive cash inflows from continuing operations.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B><I>Inflation</I></B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Our assets are, to a large extent, liquid in nature and therefore not significantly affected by
inflation. However, inflation may result in increases in our expenses, such as employee
compensation, advertising and promotional costs, and office occupancy costs. To the extent
inflation, or the expectation thereof, results in rising interest rates or has other adverse
effects upon the securities markets and on the value of financial instruments, it may adversely
affect our financial condition and results of operations. A substantial decline in the value of
fixed-income or equity investments could adversely affect the net asset value of funds and accounts
we manage, which in turn would result in a decline in investment advisory and performance fee
revenue.
</DIV>


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->35<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>1.&nbsp;&nbsp;SUMMARY OF SIGNIFICANT ACCOUNTING POLICIES</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>General Information and Basis of Presentation</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The consolidated financial statements include the accounts of Nuveen Investments, Inc. (&#147;the
Company&#148; or &#147;Nuveen Investments&#148;) and its majority-owned subsidiaries and have been prepared in
conformity with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America. All
significant intercompany transactions and accounts have been eliminated in consolidation.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Nuveen Investments markets its highly specialized investment teams, each with its own brand name
and area of expertise: NWQ, specializing in value-style equities; Nuveen, focused on fixed-income
investments; Santa Barbara, committed to growth equities; Tradewinds, specializing in global
equities; Rittenhouse, dedicated to &#147;blue-chip&#148; growth equities; and Symphony, with expertise in
alternative investments as well as equity and credit strategies.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Operations of Nuveen Investments are organized around its principal advisory subsidiaries, which
are registered investment advisers under the Investment Advisers Act of 1940. These advisory
subsidiaries manage the Nuveen mutual funds and closed-end funds and provide investment services
for individual and institutional managed accounts. Additionally, Nuveen Investments, LLC, a
registered broker and dealer in securities under the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, provides
investment product distribution and related services for the Company&#146;s managed funds.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Sale of The St. Paul Travelers Companies, Inc.&#146;s Ownership Interest in Nuveen Investments</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On April&nbsp;7, 2005, The St. Paul Travelers Companies, Inc. (&#147;STA&#148;) sold approximately 40
million shares of Nuveen Investments&#146; common stock in a secondary underwritten public offering at
$34.00 per share.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In addition, the Company repurchased $600&nbsp;million of Nuveen Investments common stock directly from
STA at a price of $32.98 per share, or approximately 18.2&nbsp;million shares. The repurchase of these
shares was completed through two steps &#151; a $200&nbsp;million (6.0&nbsp;million shares) repurchase was
completed on April&nbsp;7, 2005, and a $400&nbsp;million forward purchase (plus interest) was settled on July
28, 2005. The entire $600&nbsp;million repurchase has been recorded by Nuveen Investments as if it were
completed in its entirety on April&nbsp;7, 2005. As such, effective April&nbsp;7, 2005, Nuveen Investments
had approximately 75.9&nbsp;million shares of common stock outstanding for the purpose of computing
basic earnings per share. Upon the closing of the secondary offering, the Company was no longer a
majority-owned subsidiary of STA, and, as of the end of September&nbsp;2005, all of STA&#146;s remaining
ownership interest had been sold.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Expensing Stock Options</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Effective April&nbsp;1, 2004, the Company began expensing the cost of stock options in accordance with
the fair value recognition provisions of Statement of Financial Accounting Standards (&#147;SFAS&#148;) No.
123, &#147;Accounting for Stock-Based Compensation.&#148; Under the fair value recognition provisions of
SFAS No.&nbsp;123, stock-based compensation cost is measured at the grant date based on the value of the
award and is recognized as expense over the lesser of the options&#146; vesting period or the related
employee service period. A Black-Scholes option-pricing model was used to determine the fair value
of each award at the time of the grant.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The retroactive restatement method described in SFAS No.&nbsp;148, &#147;Accounting for Stock-Based
Compensation &#151; Transition and Disclosure&#148; was adopted and the results for prior years have been
restated. Compensation cost recognized is the same as that which would have been recognized had
the fair value method of SFAS No.&nbsp;123 been applied from its original effective date. Prior to
April&nbsp;1, 2004, the Company accounted for stock option plans under the provisions of APB Opinion No.
25, &#147;Accounting for Stock Issued to Employees&#148; and related interpretations.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In December&nbsp;2004, the Financial Accounting Standards Board (&#147;FASB&#148;) issued SFAS No.&nbsp;123 (Revised
2004), &#147;Share-Based Payment&#148; (&#147;SFAS No.&nbsp;123R&#148;). SFAS No.&nbsp;123R is a revision of SFAS No.&nbsp;123, and
supersedes APB Opinion No.&nbsp;25 and its related implementation guidance. SFAS No.&nbsp;123R focuses
primarily
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->40<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">



<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">on accounting for transactions in which an entity obtains employee services through share-based
payment transactions. SFAS No.&nbsp;123R requires a public entity to measure the cost of employee
services received in exchange for the award of equity instruments based on the fair value of the
award at the date of grant. The cost will be recognized over the period during which an employee
is required to provide services in exchange for the award. SFAS No.&nbsp;123R requires the use of a
slightly different method of accounting for forfeitures. Beginning in 2006, the Company adopted
SFAS No.&nbsp;123R. No cumulative accounting adjustment was recorded, as this change in methodology did
not have a material impact on the Company&#146;s consolidated financial statements.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Other</I><BR>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Certain other amounts in the prior year financial statements have been reclassified to conform to
the 2006 presentation. These reclassifications had no effect on net income or stockholders&#146; equity.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Use of Estimates</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">These financial statements rely, in part, on estimates. Actual results could differ from these
estimates. In the opinion of management, all necessary adjustments (consisting of normal recurring
accruals) have been reflected for a fair presentation of the results of operations, financial
position and cash flows in the accompanying consolidated financial statements.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Cash and Cash Equivalents</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Cash and cash equivalents include cash on hand, investment instruments with maturities of three
months or less and other highly liquid investments, including commercial paper and money market
funds, which are readily convertible to cash. Amounts presented on our consolidated balance sheets
approximate fair value. Included in cash and cash equivalents are approximately $5&nbsp;million of
treasury bills segregated in a special reserve account for the benefit of customers under rule
15c3-3 of the Securities and Exchange Commission.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Securities Purchased Under Agreements to Resell</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Securities purchased under agreements to resell are treated as collateralized financing
transactions and are carried at the amounts at which such securities will be subsequently resold,
including accrued interest, and approximate fair value. The Company&#146;s exposure to credit risks
associated with the nonperformance of counterparties in fulfilling these contractual obligations
can be directly impacted by market fluctuations that may impair the counterparties&#146; ability to
satisfy their obligations. It is the Company&#146;s policy to take possession of the securities
underlying the agreements to resell or enter into tri-party agreements, which include segregation
of the collateral by an independent third party for the benefit of the Company. The Company
monitors the value of these securities daily and, if necessary, obtains additional collateral to
assure that the agreements are fully secured. At December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005, the Company had
approximately $50&nbsp;million and $20&nbsp;million, respectively, in securities purchased under agreements
to resell.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company utilizes resale agreements to invest cash not required to fund daily operations. The
level of such investments will fluctuate on a daily basis. Such resale agreements typically mature
on the day following the day on which the Company enters into such agreements. Since these
agreements are highly liquid investments, readily convertible to cash, and mature in less than
three months, the Company includes these amounts in cash equivalents for balance sheet and cash
flow purposes.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Securities Transactions</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Securities transactions entered into by the Company&#146;s broker-dealer subsidiary are recorded on a
settlement date basis, which is generally three business days after the trade date. Securities
owned are valued at market value with profit and loss accrued on unsettled transactions based on
the trade date.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Furniture, Equipment and Leasehold Improvements</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Furniture and equipment, primarily computer equipment, is depreciated on a straight-line basis over
estimated useful lives ranging from three to ten years. Leasehold improvements are amortized over
the lesser of the economic useful life of the improvement or the remaining term of the lease. The
Company capitalizes certain
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->41<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">



<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">costs incurred in the development of internal-use software. Software development costs are
amortized over a period of not more than five years.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Investments</I><BR>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Realized gains on the sale of investments are calculated based on the specific identification
method and are recorded in &#147;Other Income/Expense&#148; on the accompanying consolidated statements of
income.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Investments consist of securities classified as either: non-marketable, trading, or
available-for-sale.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Of the
approximate $129&nbsp;million in total investments at
December&nbsp;31, 2006, approximately $55 million relates to
equity-based funds and accounts and $74&nbsp;million relates to fixed-income funds or
accounts.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Also included in total investments of $129&nbsp;million and $121&nbsp;million as of December&nbsp;31, 2006 and
2005, respectively, on the accompanying consolidated balance sheets are underlying securities from
three funds managed by the Company (see Note 12, &#147;Consolidated Funds&#148;). These underlying
securities approximate $35&nbsp;million and $28&nbsp;million as of December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005, respectively,
and are excluded from the discussion, below, regarding the Company&#146;s classification of investments
as either non-marketable, trading, or available-for sale. As a result of being the sole investor
in the three funds referenced above at December&nbsp;31, 2005 and the majority investor as of December
31, 2006, the Company is required to consolidate these funds in its consolidated financial
statements. Although the underlying securities of these fund investments would be classified as
&#147;trading&#148; securities by the funds if the funds were to follow SFAS No.&nbsp;115, &#147;Accounting for Certain
Investments in Debt and Equity Securities,&#148; the Company does not classify these underlying
securities as &#147;trading&#148; securities, as the Company&#146;s investment is at the fund level. In addition,
the Company&#146;s objective for holding an investment in these three funds is not to buy or sell
frequently nor is it to generate profits. The Company&#146;s objective is to hold the fund investments
until such time that they are majority-owned by outside investors.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Non-marketable securities are investments that are saleable, but for which no ready market exists.
These investments are carried at cost. At December&nbsp;31, 2006, the Company did not hold any
investments that it classified as non-marketable. At December&nbsp;31, 2005, approximately $30&nbsp;million
of the Company&#146;s total investments were classified as non-marketable, which represented non-voting
common stock in a privately held institutional equity manager (Institutional Capital Corporation).
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Trading securities are securities bought and held principally for the purpose of selling them in
the near term. These investments are reported at fair value, with unrealized gains and losses
included in earnings. At December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005, approximately $27&nbsp;million and $22&nbsp;million of
investments, respectively, were classified as trading securities. As of December&nbsp;31, 2006 and
2005, approximately $12&nbsp;million and $11&nbsp;million of these securities, respectively, were in products
or portfolios that are not currently marketed by the Company but may be offered to investors in the
future. The fair value for these products is determined through a combination of quoted market
prices as well as a valuation of any derivatives employed by means of discounted cash flow
analysis. The remaining balance of approximately $14&nbsp;million and $10&nbsp;million as of December&nbsp;31,
2006 and 2005, respectively, included as trading securities is our investment in certain
Company-sponsored mutual funds. The purpose of these investments is to mitigate the Company&#146;s
interest rate exposure for those participants in the deferred compensation program who have elected
to defer compensation with such deferred compensation earning interest based on the rate of return
of one of several managed funds sponsored by the Company. To mitigate exposure and to minimize the
volatility of the Company&#146;s deferred compensation liability, the Company purchases shares of the
underlying funds at the time of the deferral.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Investments not classified as either non-marketable or trading are classified as available-for-sale
securities. These investments are carried at fair value with unrealized holding gains and losses
reported net of tax as a separate component of accumulated other comprehensive income until
realized. Realized gains and losses are reflected as a component of non-operating
income/(expense). At December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005, approximately $66&nbsp;million and $40&nbsp;million of
investments, respectively, were classified as available-for-sale and consist
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->42<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company periodically evaluates its investments for other-than-temporary declines in value.
Other-than-temporary declines in value may exist when the fair value of an investment security has
been below the carrying value for an extended period of time. If an other-than-temporary decline
in value is determined to exist, the unrealized investment loss net of tax in accumulated other
comprehensive income is realized as a charge to net income in that period. At December&nbsp;31, 2006,
for the six investments that have unrealized losses for greater than 12&nbsp;months, the Company
believes that all of these unrealized losses are only temporary and are due to temporary market
conditions. Supporting this conclusion is the increase in the value of these investments, and
commensurate decline in total unrealized losses at December&nbsp;31, 2006, compared to total unrealized
losses at December&nbsp;31, 2005. The following table presents information about the Company&#146;s
investments with unrealized losses at December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005 (in 000s):

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Revenue Recognition</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Investment advisory fees from assets under management are recognized ratably over the period that
assets are under management. Performance fees are recognized only at the performance measurement
dates contained in the individual account management agreements and are dependent upon performance
of the account exceeding agreed-upon benchmarks over the relevant period. Some of the Company&#146;s
investment management agreements provide that, to the extent certain enumerated expenses exceed a
specified percentage of a fund&#146;s
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->43<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">



<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">or a portfolio&#146;s average net assets for a given year, the advisor will absorb such expenses through
a reduction in management fees. Investment advisory fees are recorded net of any such expense
reductions. Investment advisory fees are also recorded net of any sub-advisory fees paid by the
Company based on the terms of those arrangements.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Accumulated Other Comprehensive Income/(Loss)</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company&#146;s other comprehensive income/(loss) consists of: changes in unrealized gains and
losses on certain investment securities classified as available-for-sale (recorded net of tax);
reclassification adjustments for realized gains/(losses) on those investment securities classified
as available-for-sale; activity from terminated cash flow hedges; activity related to the Company&#146;s
qualified pension and post-retirement plans; and foreign currency translation adjustments.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The
changes in unrealized gains and (losses) (net of tax) on certain investment securities classified
as available-for-sale were approximately $0.9&nbsp;million, ($0.3&nbsp;million) and $3.2&nbsp;million for the
years ended December&nbsp;31, 2006, 2005, and 2004, respectively. The related cumulative tax effects of
the changes in unrealized gains and losses on those investment securities classified as
available-for-sale were deferred tax benefits/(liabilities) of ($0.3&nbsp;million) in 2006, $0.2&nbsp;million
in 2005 and ($2.1&nbsp;million) in 2004. The reclassification adjustments for realized gains/(losses)
for those investment securities classified as available-for-sale resulted in gains of approximately
$3.3&nbsp;million, $2.2&nbsp;million and $0.1&nbsp;million in 2006, 2005 and 2004, respectively.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">During
2006, the Company did not have any new activity resulting from cash flow hedges. During 2005, the
Company had two different sources of activity from terminated cash flow hedges: (1)&nbsp;the
acceleration of the amortization of the deferred loss resulting from a series of Treasury rate lock
transactions related to the private placement debt; and (2)&nbsp;the deferral of a gain and its related
amortization resulting from a series of Treasury rate lock transactions related to the Senior Term
Notes.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The first source of 2005 activity from terminated cash flow hedges relates to the private placement
debt. As discussed further in Note 5, &#147;Derivative Financial Instruments,&#148; the Company had incurred
a deferred loss during 2003 in connection with a series of Treasury rate lock transactions that had
been entered into in anticipation of the private placement debt (see Note 4, &#147;Debt&#148;). This loss
was being reclassified into current earnings commensurate with the recognition of interest expense
on the private placement debt. The amortization of this loss was approximately $0.1&nbsp;million and
$0.3&nbsp;million for the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2003 and 2004, respectively. At December&nbsp;31, 2004,
the remaining unamortized loss from these Treasury rate lock transactions was approximately $1.1
million. On April&nbsp;6, 2005, the Company made an early repayment of the entire $300&nbsp;million of
private placement debt. As a result of this early repayment, the Company accelerated the
recognition of the remaining $1.1&nbsp;million of unamortized deferred loss relating to those Treasury
rate lock transactions. At December&nbsp;31, 2005, there was no remaining unamortized loss relating to
these Treasury rate lock transactions.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The second source of 2005 activity from terminated cash flow hedges relates to the Senior Term
Notes. As discussed further in Note 5, &#147;Derivative Financial Instruments,&#148; during 2005, the
Company deferred a $1.6&nbsp;million gain that resulted from another series of Treasury rate lock
transactions; these Treasury rate lock transactions were entered into in anticipation of the
issuance of the Senior Term Notes (see Note 4, &#147;Debt,&#148; for additional information). This $1.6
million gain is being reclassified into current earnings commensurate with the recognition of
interest expense on the 5-year and 10-year term debt. As the gain resulting from these Treasury
rate lock transactions did not occur until 2005, there was no amortization for the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2004. For the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2005 and 2006, approximately $0.1&nbsp;million and
$0.2&nbsp;million of this gain, respectively, were reclassified from deferred gain in other
comprehensive income to a reduction of interest expense. At December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005, the
remaining unamortized gain on these Treasury rate lock transactions approximated $1.3&nbsp;million and
$1.5&nbsp;million, respectively. During 2007, the Company expects to reclassify approximately $0.3
million of the deferred gain into interest expense.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The next component of the Company&#146;s other comprehensive income/(loss) relates to the Company&#146;s
pension and post-retirement plans. For the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2005, the Company updated
certain actuarial
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->44<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">



<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">assumptions used to determine the accumulated benefit obligation (&#147;ABO&#148;) for its qualified pension
plan. As a result, the Company&#146;s qualified pension plan was determined to be underfunded on an ABO
basis as of December&nbsp;31, 2005. Consequently, a charge was recorded to stockholders&#146; equity, net of
income tax benefits, as a component of other comprehensive loss, of approximately $2.4&nbsp;million. On
September&nbsp;29, 2006, the FASB issued a new pension standard, SFAS No.&nbsp;158, &#147;Employers&#146; Accounting
for Defined Benefit Pension and Other Postretirement Plans&#148; (&#147;SFAS No.&nbsp;158&#148;). (See Note 8,
&#147;Retirement Plans,&#148; for additional information.) At December&nbsp;31, 2006, an additional charge was
recorded to stockholders&#146; equity, net of income tax benefits, as a component of other comprehensive
loss, of approximately $2.2&nbsp;million for the Company&#146;s qualified and excess pension plans. In
addition, at December&nbsp;31, 2006, a gain of approximately $75,000 was recorded as a component of
other comprehensive income related to the Company&#146;s post-retirement benefits plan.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Finally, the last component of the Company&#146;s other comprehensive income/(loss) relates to foreign
currency translation adjustments. For the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2006, approximately $3,000 of a
foreign currency translation loss was recorded into other comprehensive income. The Company
recorded approximately $1,000 of foreign currency translation gains for each of the years ended
December&nbsp;31, 2005 and 2004.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company&#146;s total comprehensive income was approximately $185.7&nbsp;million in 2006, $171.1&nbsp;million
in 2005, and $159.9&nbsp;million in 2004.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Goodwill</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In July&nbsp;2001, the FASB issued Statement SFAS No.&nbsp;142, &#147;Goodwill and Other Intangible Assets&#148; (&#147;SFAS
No.&nbsp;142&#148;.) SFAS No.&nbsp;142 requires that goodwill and intangible assets with indefinite useful lives
no longer be amortized, but instead that they be tested for impairment at least annually using a
two-step process. Other intangible assets continue to be amortized over their useful lives.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company has chosen May&nbsp;31 as its measurement date for the annual SFAS No.&nbsp;142 impairment test.
Neither the initial SFAS No.&nbsp;142 impairment test (as of January&nbsp;1, 2002), nor any of the
subsequent, ongoing annual SFAS No.&nbsp;142 impairment tests (as of May&nbsp;31) indicate any impairment of
goodwill. The Company has identified five reporting units for purposes of the impairment test.
These reporting units are one level below our operating segment and were determined based on how we
manage our business, including our internal reporting structure, management accountability and
resource prioritization process. The Company&#146;s SFAS No.&nbsp;142 goodwill impairment test involves the
use of estimates. Specifically, estimates are used in assigning assets and liabilities to
reporting units, assigning goodwill to reporting units and determining the fair value of reporting
units. While we believe that our testing was appropriate, the use of different assumptions may
have resulted in recognizing some impairment of goodwill in our financial statements.
</DIV>

December&nbsp;31, 2006, as presented on our consolidated balance sheets:

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Other Receivables and Other Liabilities</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Included in other receivables and other liabilities are receivables from and payables to
broker-dealers and customers, primarily in conjunction with unsettled trades. These receivables
were approximately $2.0&nbsp;million and $9.0&nbsp;million, and these payables were approximately $0.9
million and $4.6&nbsp;million at December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005, respectively.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Other Assets</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">At December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005, other assets consist primarily of approximately $11.7&nbsp;million and
$14.6&nbsp;million, respectively, in commissions advanced by the Company on sales of certain mutual fund
shares. Advanced sales commission costs are being amortized over the lesser of the Securities and
Exchange Commission Rule&nbsp;12b-1 revenue stream period (one to eight years) or the period during
which the shares of the fund upon which the commissions were paid remain outstanding.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Fair Value of Financial Instruments</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">SFAS No.&nbsp;107, &#147;Disclosures About Fair Value of Financial Instruments&#148; (&#147;SFAS No.&nbsp;107&#148;) requires the
disclosure of the estimated fair value of financial instruments. The fair value of a financial
instrument is the amount at which the instrument could be exchanged in a current transaction
between willing parties, other than in a forced or liquidation sale.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In determining the fair value of its financial instruments, the Company uses a variety of methods
and assumptions that are based on market conditions and risk existing at each balance sheet date.
For the majority of financial instruments, including most derivatives, long-term investments and
long-term debt, standard market conventions and techniques such as discounted cash flow analysis,
option pricing models, replacement cost and termination cost are used to determine fair value.
Dealer quotes are used for the remaining financial instruments. All methods of assessing fair
value result in a general approximation of value, and such value may never actually be realized.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Cash and cash equivalents, marketable securities, notes and other accounts receivable and
investments are financial assets with carrying values that approximate fair value because of the
short maturity of those instruments. Accounts payable and other accrued expenses are financial
liabilities with carrying values that also approximate fair value because of the short maturity of
those instruments. The fair value of long-term debt is based on market prices.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">A comparison of the fair values and carrying amounts of these instruments is as follows:
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Leases</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company leases its various office locations under cancelable and non-cancelable
operating leases, whose initial terms typically range from month-to-month to fifteen years, along
with options that permit renewals for additional periods. Minimum rent is expensed on a
straight-line basis over the term of the lease, with any applicable leasehold incentives applied as
a reduction to monthly lease expense.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Advertising and Promotional Costs</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Advertising and promotional costs include amounts related to the marketing and distribution of
specific products offered by the Company as well as expenses associated with promoting the
Company&#146;s brands and image. The Company&#146;s policy is to expense such costs as incurred.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Other Income/(Expense)</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Other income/(expense) includes realized gains and losses on investments and miscellaneous income,
including gain or loss on the disposal of property.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The following is a summary of Other Income/(Expense) for the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2006, 2005
and 2004:

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Total other income/(expense) for 2006 was $15.7&nbsp;million. Included in the $15.5&nbsp;million of gains on
sale of investments is approximately $10.1&nbsp;million related to the sale of the Company&#146;s investment
in Institutional Capital Corporation. Gains from sales of investments also include approximately
$4.8&nbsp;million recognized on the sale of seed investments in Company sponsored funds and accounts.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Total other income/(expense) was $7.9&nbsp;million in 2005. As a result of the early repayment of the
private placement debt, the Company accelerated the recognition of unamortized deferred gains and
losses resulting from various interest rate hedging activity associated with the private placement
debt. This accelerated recognition resulted in $3.6&nbsp;million of miscellaneous income for the year.
Supplementing this other income was $4.8&nbsp;million in gains recognized on the sale of seed
investments.
</DIV>

<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Total net interest expense increased $9.2&nbsp;million for the year due to increased interest expense as
a result of increased debt associated with the repurchase of shares from STA. Partially offsetting
this increase was an increase in interest income due to interest earned on investable cash.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Net interest expense increased $11.0&nbsp;million in 2005 as a result of increase debt associated with
the repurchase of shares from STA. Partially offsetting this increase was an increase in dividends
and interest income due to dividends received during 2005 and interest earned on the consolidated
funds.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Taxes</I><BR>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company and its subsidiaries file a consolidated federal income tax return. The Company
provides for income taxes on a separate return basis. Under this method, deferred tax assets and
liabilities are determined based on differences between financial reporting and the tax bases of
assets and liabilities and are measured using the enacted tax rates and laws that are applicable to
periods in which the differences are expected to affect taxable income. Although valuation
allowances may be established, when necessary, to reduce deferred tax assets to amounts expected to
be realized, there were no deferred tax asset valuation allowances at December&nbsp;31, 2006 or 2005.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Supplemental Cash Flow Information</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company paid cash interest of $36.7&nbsp;million in 2006, $21.7&nbsp;million in 2005 and $12.6&nbsp;million in
2004. This compares with interest expense reported in the Company&#146;s consolidated statements of
income of $39.6&nbsp;million, $27.9&nbsp;million and $12.5&nbsp;million for the respective reporting years.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Federal and state income taxes paid in the years ending December&nbsp;31, 2006, 2005 and 2004, amounting
to approximately $101.9&nbsp;million, $85.9&nbsp;million and $92.6&nbsp;million, respectively, include required
payments on estimated taxable income and final payments of prior year taxes required to be paid
upon filing the final federal and state tax returns, reduced by refunds received.
</DIV>
