<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>
<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Options to purchase 6,369 shares of the Company&#146;s common stock were outstanding as of December&nbsp;31,
2006, but were not included in the computation of diluted earnings per share because their
inclusion would have been antidilutive since the options&#146; weighted average exercise price of $50.82
per share was greater than the average market price of $47.25 for the Company&#146;s common shares
during the applicable period. At December&nbsp;31, 2005, all options to purchase shares of the
Company&#146;s common stock outstanding were included in the computation of diluted earnings per share
because all of the options&#146; respective exercise price per share was less than the average market
price of the Company&#146;s common shares during the applicable period. At December&nbsp;31, 2004, options
to purchase 103,437 shares of the Company&#146;s common stock at a price range of $34.40 to $39.47 per
share were outstanding, but were not included in the computation of diluted earnings per share
because the options&#146; respective exercise price per share was greater than the average market price
of the Company&#146;s common shares during the applicable period.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Private Placement Debt</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On September&nbsp;19, 2003, the Company issued $300&nbsp;million of senior unsecured notes (the &#147;private
placement debt&#148;). These notes carried a fixed coupon rate of 4.22%, payable semi-annually and were
issued at 100% of par, unsecured, and prepayable at any time in whole or in part. In the event of
prepayment, the Company would pay an amount equal to par plus accrued interest plus a &#147;make-whole
premium,&#148; if applicable. Proceeds from the private placement debt were used to refinance existing
debt and for general corporate purposes. These notes were originally scheduled to mature on
September&nbsp;19, 2008, but were repaid on April&nbsp;6, 2005, with borrowings made under a Bridge
Credit Agreement (discussed below). At the time of the repayment, the Company also paid
approximately $1.5&nbsp;million in accrued interest. Under the terms of the private placement debt, no
&#147;make-whole premium&#148; amounts were due. As a result of the repayment, there were no amounts
outstanding at December&nbsp;31, 2005.
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->51<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Bridge Credit Facility</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On April&nbsp;1, 2005, Nuveen Investments entered into a $750&nbsp;million bridge credit agreement with
various financial institutions. The maturity date of this credit agreement was March&nbsp;31, 2006.
Borrowings under this facility bore an interest rate, at the Company&#146;s option, of either LIBOR or
the Federal Funds rate plus a spread equal to 0.335% to 0.470% based on Nuveen Investments&#146;
leverage, with such applicable spread increasing by 0.25% on September&nbsp;30, 2005, and by an
additional 0.25% on December&nbsp;31, 2005. During the second quarter of 2005, the Company had used
approximately $300&nbsp;million of the amount available under the facility to prepay the holders of the
Company&#146;s 4.22% senior unsecured notes due September&nbsp;19, 2008. During the third quarter of 2005,
the Company used approximately $410&nbsp;million of the remaining amount available under the bridge
credit agreement primarily to fulfill its forward contract obligation to repurchase shares of its
capital stock owned by STA (refer to Note 1, &#147;Sale of The St. Paul Travelers Companies, Inc.&#146;s
Ownership Interest in Nuveen Investments&#148;). During the third quarter of 2005, the entire $710
million borrowed under the bridge credit agreement was repaid with
borrowings made under a senior revolving credit facility and the issuance of senior notes (both discussed below) and the bridge
credit agreement was terminated.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Senior Term Notes</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On September&nbsp;12, 2005, Nuveen Investments issued $550&nbsp;million of senior unsecured notes, comprised
of $250&nbsp;million of 5-year notes and $300&nbsp;million of 10-year notes. The Company received
approximately $544&nbsp;million in net proceeds after discounts and other debt issuance costs. The
5-year senior notes bear interest at an annual fixed rate of 5.0% payable semi-annually beginning
March&nbsp;15, 2006. The 10-year senior notes bear interest at an annual fixed rate of 5.5% payable
semi-annually also beginning March&nbsp;15, 2006. The net proceeds from the notes were used to repay a
portion of the outstanding debt under the bridge credit facility. The costs related to the
issuance of the senior term notes are being capitalized and amortized to expense over their term.
At December&nbsp;31, 2006, the fair value of the 5-year and 10-year senior term notes was approximately
$245.2&nbsp;million and $288.0&nbsp;million, respectively.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Senior Revolving Credit Facility</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In addition to the senior term notes, the Company has a $400&nbsp;million senior revolving credit
facility that expires on September&nbsp;15, 2010. As of December&nbsp;31, 2005, the Company had borrowed
$150&nbsp;million of the total amount available under the senior revolving credit facility, with the
majority of the proceeds being used to repay the amount due under the bridge credit facility (refer
to discussion above). During the second quarter of 2006, the Company repaid $50&nbsp;million of the
amount borrowed under this senior revolving credit facility. At December&nbsp;31, 2006 the Company had
$100&nbsp;million outstanding under this facility. The rate of interest payable under the new senior
revolving credit facility is, at the Company&#146;s option, a function of either one of various floating
rate indices or the Federal Funds rate. For the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005, the
weighted- average interest rate on the amount borrowed under the senior revolving credit facility
was 5.46% and 4.54%, respectively. The agreement also requires the Company to pay a facility fee
at an annual rate of a range of 0.08% to 0.15% that is dependent on our debt rating. Proceeds from
borrowings under this facility may be used for fulfilling day-to-day cash requirements and general
corporate purposes, including acquisitions, share repurchases and asset purchases.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Other</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company&#146;s broker-dealer subsidiary may utilize available, uncommitted lines of credit with no
annual facility fees, which approximate $50&nbsp;million, to satisfy unanticipated, short-term liquidity
needs. At December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005, no borrowings were outstanding on these uncommitted lines of
credit.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>5.&nbsp;&nbsp;DERIVATIVE FINANCIAL INSTRUMENTS</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">SFAS No.&nbsp;133, &#147;Accounting for Derivative Instruments and Hedging Activities,&#148; as amended by SFAS
No.&nbsp;138, &#147;Accounting for Certain Derivative Instruments and Certain Hedging Activities, an
Amendment of FASB Statement No.&nbsp;133&#148; and further amended by SFAS No.&nbsp;149, &#147;Amendment of Statement
133 on Derivative Instruments and Hedging Activities,&#148; (collectively, &#147;SFAS No.&nbsp;133&#148;) states that,
unless a derivative qualifies as a hedge, the gain or loss from a derivative instrument must be
recorded currently into earnings. Under
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->52<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">



<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">SFAS No.&nbsp;133, three types of hedges are recognized: fair value hedges, cash flow hedges, and
hedges of a corporation&#146;s net investments in foreign operations.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Fair value hedges </I>An entity may designate a derivative instrument as hedging the exposure to
changes in the fair value (market value) of financial assets or liabilities. For example, a
fixed-rate bond&#146;s market value changes when prevailing market interest rates change. Hedging the
fixed-rate bond&#146;s price risk with a derivative would be considered a fair value hedge.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Cash flow hedges </I>An entity may also designate a derivative instrument as hedging the exposure to
variability in expected future cash flows that is attributable to a particular risk. That exposure
may be associated with an existing recognized asset or liability or a forecasted transaction.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Derivative Financial Instruments Related to Private Placement Debt</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In August&nbsp;2004, in anticipation of the private placement debt issuance, the Company entered into a
series of Treasury rate lock transactions with an aggregate notional amount of $100&nbsp;million. These
Treasury rate locks were accounted for as cash-flow hedges, as they hedged against the variability
in future projected interest payments on the then-forecasted issuance of fixed-rate debt (the
private placement debt) attributable to changes in interest rates. The prevailing Treasury rates
had declined by the time of the private placement debt issuance and the locks were settled for a
payment by the Company of $1.5&nbsp;million. The Company had recorded this loss in &#147;Accumulated Other
Comprehensive Income/(Loss)&#148; in the accompanying consolidated balance sheets, as the Treasury rate
locks were considered highly effective for accounting purposes in mitigating the interest rate risk
on the forecasted debt issuance. Amounts accumulated in other comprehensive loss were to be
reclassified into earnings commensurate with the recognition of the interest expense on the private
placement debt. During the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2004, the Company reclassified approximately
$0.3&nbsp;million of the loss on the Treasury rate lock transactions into interest expense. At December
31, 2004, the remaining unamortized loss on these Treasury rate lock transactions was approximately
$1.1&nbsp;million. On April&nbsp;6, 2005, the Company repaid the entire $300&nbsp;million of private placement
debt (refer to Note 4, &#147;Debt&#148;). As a result of the early repayment of the private placement debt,
the Company accelerated the recognition of the remaining approximate $1.1&nbsp;million of unamortized
deferred loss resulting from these Treasury rate lock transactions. Due to the accelerated
recognition of the deferred loss, there was no remaining unamortized loss on these Treasury rate
lock transactions at December&nbsp;31, 2005.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Also related to the private placement debt, the Company entered into a series of interest rate swap
transactions during 2003. The Company entered into forward-starting interest rate swap
transactions as hedges against changes in a portion of the fair value of the private placement
debt. Under the agreements, payments were to be exchanged at specified intervals based on fixed
and floating interest rates. All of the interest rate swap transactions were designated as fair
value hedges to mitigate the changes in fair value of the hedged portion of the private placement
debt. The Company determined that these interest rate swap transactions qualified for treatment
under the short-cut method of SFAS No.&nbsp;133 of measuring effectiveness. All of these interest rate
swap transactions were cancelled. The cancellation of these interest rate swap transactions
resulted in a total gain to the Company of $8.1&nbsp;million. These gains were being amortized over the
term of the private placement debt, lowering the effective interest rate of the private placement
debt. The amortization of the gains resulting from the cancellation of these interest rate swap
transactions is reflected in &#147;Interest Expense&#148; on the accompanying consolidated statements of
income. Approximately $1.3&nbsp;million of these gains were amortized as a reduction to interest
expense for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2004. As a result of the early repayment of the private
placement debt on April&nbsp;6, 2005, the Company accelerated the recognition of the remaining
unamortized gains resulting from the interest rate swap transactions. For the year ended December
31, 2005, approximately $6.6&nbsp;million of gains from the cancellation of interest rate swap
agreements was recognized as current income. Due to the accelerated recognition of these gains,
there was no remaining unamortized gain on interest rate swap transactions at December&nbsp;31, 2005.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In addition to amortizing the deferred gains and losses on the derivative transactions, the Company
was amortizing debt issuance costs related to the private placement debt. On April&nbsp;6, 2005, there
was a total of $1.5&nbsp;million in unamortized private placement fees. Due to the repayment of the
private placement debt, the
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->53<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">



<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">recognition of these fees was also accelerated. The total net resulting gain from the acceleration
of the Treasury rate lock transactions, the cancellation of the interest rate swaps and the private
placement fees was approximately $3.6&nbsp;million. This gain was recorded as Other Income/(Expense) in
2005.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Derivative Financial Instruments Related to Senior Term Notes</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In anticipation of the issuance of the senior term notes (refer to Note 4, &#147;Debt&#148;), the Company
entered into a series of Treasury rate lock transactions with an aggregate notional amount of $550
million. These Treasury rate locks were accounted for as cash-flow hedges, as they hedged against
the variability in future projected interest payments on the forecasted issuance of fixed-rate debt
(the longer-term senior term notes that replaced the bridge credit agreement) attributable to
changes in interest rates. The prevailing Treasury rates had increased by the time of the senior
term notes issuance and the locks were settled for a net payment to the Company of approximately
$1.6&nbsp;million. The Company has recorded this gain in &#147;Accumulated Other Comprehensive
Income/(Loss)&#148; on the accompanying consolidated balance sheets as of December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005, as
the Treasury rate locks were considered highly effective for accounting purposes in mitigating the
interest rate risk on the forecasted debt issuance. The $1.6&nbsp;million is being reclassified into
current earnings commensurate with the recognition of interest expense on the 5-year and 10-year
term debt. For the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005, approximately $241,000 and $68,000,
respectively, of the deferred gain was amortized into interest expense. At December&nbsp;31, 2006 and
2005, the unamortized gain on the Treasury rate lock transactions was approximately $1.3&nbsp;million
and $1.5&nbsp;million, respectively. During 2007, the Company expects to reclassify approximately
$253,000 of the deferred gain on the Treasury rate lock transactions into interest expense.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Other Derivative Financial Instruments</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Also included in the accompanying consolidated balance sheets as of December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005 are
certain swap agreements and futures contracts that have not been designated as hedging instruments.
These swap agreements and futures contracts are being used to mitigate overall market risk of
certain recently created product portfolios that are not yet being marketed. At December&nbsp;31, 2006
and 2005, the net fair value of these open non-hedging derivatives was approximately $0.3&nbsp;million
and $0.3&nbsp;million, respectively, and is reflected as approximately
$259,000 in &#147;Other Assets&#148; and $601,000 in &#147;Other
Short-Term Liabilities&#148; on the accompanying consolidated balance
sheet as of December&nbsp;31, 2006, and $300,000 in &#147;Other
Short-Term Liabilities&#148; on the accompanying consolidated balance
sheet as of December&nbsp;31, 2005. For the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2006, the Company
recorded approximately $902,000 in losses from these derivatives, approximately $539,000 of which
were realized losses and the remainder unrealized. For the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2005, the
Company recorded approximately $805,000 in losses from these derivatives, approximately $591,000 of
which were realized losses and the remainder unrealized. Realized gains and losses and unrealized
gains and losses from these derivatives are reflected in &#147;Other income/(expense)&#148; on the
accompanying consolidated statements of income. These losses were offset by gains on the product
portfolios referenced above.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>6.&nbsp;&nbsp;EQUITY PROGRAMS</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>NWQ</I>

</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">As part of the NWQ acquisition, key management purchased a non-controlling, member interest in NWQ
Investment Management Company, LLC. The non-controlling interest of $0.3&nbsp;million as of December
31, 2006, and $0.4&nbsp;million as of December&nbsp;31, 2005, is reflected in minority interest on the
consolidated balance sheets. This purchase allows management to participate in profits of NWQ
above specified levels beginning January&nbsp;1, 2003. During 2006 and 2005, the Company recorded
approximately $3.8&nbsp;million and $5.6&nbsp;million, respectively, of minority interest expense, which
reflects the portion of profits applicable to the minority owners. Beginning in 2004 and
continuing through 2008, the Company has the right to purchase the non-controlling members&#146;
respective interests in NWQ at fair value. On February&nbsp;13, 2004, the Company exercised its right
to call 100% of the Class&nbsp;2 minority members&#146; interests for $15.4&nbsp;million. Of the total amount
paid, approximately $12.9&nbsp;million was recorded as goodwill. On February&nbsp;15, 2005, the Company
exercised its right to call 100% of the Class&nbsp;3 NWQ minority members&#146; interests for $22.8&nbsp;million.
Of the total amount paid, approximately $22.5&nbsp;million was recorded as goodwill. On February&nbsp;15,
2006, the Company exercised its right to call 25% of the Class&nbsp;4 NWQ minority members&#146; interests
for $22.6&nbsp;million. Of the total amount paid on March&nbsp;1, 2006, approximately $22.5&nbsp;million was
recorded as goodwill. (See Note 17, &#147;Subsequent Event.&#148;)
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->54<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Santa Barbara</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">As part of the Santa Barbara acquisition, an equity opportunity was put in place to allow key
individuals to participate in Santa Barbara&#146;s earnings growth over the next five years (Class&nbsp;2
Units, Class&nbsp;5A Units, Class&nbsp;5B Units, and Class&nbsp;6 Units, collectively referred to as &#147;Units&#148;).
The Class&nbsp;2 Units were fully vested upon issuance. The Class&nbsp;5A Units will vest one third on June
30, 2007, one third on June&nbsp;30, 2008, and one third on June&nbsp;30, 2009. One third of the Class&nbsp;5B
Units vested upon issuance, one third on June&nbsp;30, 2007, and one third on June&nbsp;30, 2009. The Class
6 Units will vest on June&nbsp;30, 2009. During 2006, the Company recorded approximately $1.2&nbsp;million
of minority interest expense, which reflects the portion of profits applicable to the minority
owners. The Units entitle the holders to receive a distribution of the cash flow from Santa
Barbara&#146;s business to the extent such cash flow exceeds certain thresholds. The distribution
thresholds vary from year to year, reflecting Santa Barbara achieving certain profit levels. The
profits interest distributions are also subject to a cap in each year. Beginning in 2008 and
continuing through 2012, the Company has the right to acquire the Units of the non-controlling
members.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>New Equity Opportunity Programs Implemented During 2006</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">During 2006, new equity opportunities were put in place covering NWQ, Tradewinds and Symphony.
These programs allow key individuals of these businesses to participate in the growth of their
respective businesses over the next five years. Classes of units were established at each
subsidiary (collectively referred to as &#147;Units&#148;). Certain of these Units vest on June&nbsp;30 of 2007,
2008, 2009, 2010 and 2011. During 2006, the Company recorded approximately $1.2&nbsp;million of
minority interest expense, which reflects the portion of profits applicable to minority owners.
The Units entitle the holders to receive a distribution of the cash flow from their business to the
extent such cash flow exceeds certain thresholds. The distribution thresholds increase from year
to year and the distributions of the profits interests are also subject to a cap in each year.
Beginning in 2008 and continuing through 2012, the Company has the right to acquire the Units of
the non-controlling members.
</DIV>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>8.&nbsp;&nbsp;RETIREMENT PLANS</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company maintains a non-contributory qualified pension plan, a non-contributory excess pension
plan (described below), and a post-retirement benefit plan. The non-contributory qualified pension
plan and the post-retirement benefit plan cover certain employees that qualify as plan
participants, excluding employees of certain of its subsidiaries. Pension benefits are based on
years of service and the employee&#146;s average compensation during the highest consecutive five years
of the employee&#146;s last ten years of employment. The Company&#146;s funding policy is to contribute
annually at least the minimum amount that can be deducted for federal income tax purposes.
Effective March&nbsp;24, 2003, the pension plans were amended to only include employees who qualified as
plan participants prior to such date. On March&nbsp;31, 2004, the plans were amended to provide that
existing plan participants will not accrue any new benefits under the plans after March&nbsp;31, 2014.
Additionally, the Company currently maintains a post-retirement benefit plan providing certain life
insurance and health care benefits for retired employees and their eligible dependents. The cost
of these benefits is shared by the Company and the retiree.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The non-contributory excess pension plan is maintained by the Company for certain employees who
participate in the qualified pension plan and whose pension benefits exceed the Section&nbsp;415
limitations of the Internal Revenue Code. Pension benefits for this plan follow the vesting
provisions of the qualified plan with new participation frozen and benefit accruals ending as
described in the prior paragraph. Funding is not made under this plan until benefits are paid,
absent a change in control of the Company.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>SFAS No.&nbsp;158</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On September&nbsp;29, 2006, the FASB issued a new pension standard, SFAS No.&nbsp;158, &#147;Employers&#146; Accounting
for Defined Benefit Pension and Other Postretirement Plans&#148; (&#147;SFAS No.&nbsp;158&#148;), marking the end of
the first phase of the FASB&#146;s project for revamping retiree-benefit accounting. For publicly
traded companies, SFAS No.&nbsp;158 is effective for fiscal years ending after December&nbsp;15, 2006. SFAS
No.&nbsp;158 requires an employer to:
</DIV>

<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt">
<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-size: 10pt">

<TR valign="top" style="font-size: 10pt; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    <TD width="2%" style="background: transparent">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD width="3%" nowrap align="left">(a)</TD>
    <TD width="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD>recognize in its statement of financial position an asset for a
plan&#146;s overfunded status or a liability for a plan&#146;s underfunded status;</TD>
</TR>

<TR>
    <TD style="font-size: 6pt">&nbsp;</TD>
</TR><TR valign="top" style="font-size: 10pt; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    <TD width="2%" style="background: transparent">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD width="3%" nowrap align="left">(b)</TD>
    <TD width="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD>measure a plan&#146;s assets and its obligations that determine its
funded status as of the end of the employer&#146;s fiscal year; and</TD>
</TR>

<TR>
    <TD style="font-size: 6pt">&nbsp;</TD>
</TR><TR valign="top" style="font-size: 10pt; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    <TD width="2%" style="background: transparent">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD width="3%" nowrap align="left">(c)</TD>
    <TD width="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD>recognize changes in the funded status of a defined benefit
post-retirement plan in the year in which the changes occur. Those
changes will be reported in comprehensive income.</TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Under SFAS No.&nbsp;158, the funded status of a pension is defined as the difference between the fair
value of a plan&#146;s assets and the projected benefit obligation (&#147;PBO&#148;). The PBO reflects
anticipated future pay increases.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">For the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2005, and prior to SFAS No.&nbsp;158, the Company had updated certain
actuarial assumptions used to determine the accumulated benefit obligation (&#147;ABO&#148;) for its
qualified pension plan. As a result, the Company&#146;s qualified pension plan was determined to be
underfunded on an ABO basis as of December&nbsp;31, 2005. Consequently, a charge was recorded to
stockholders&#146; equity, net of income tax benefits, as a component of other comprehensive loss, of
approximately $2.4&nbsp;million. At December&nbsp;31, 2006, an additional charge was recorded to
stockholders&#146; equity, net of income tax benefits, as a component of other comprehensive loss, of
approximately $2.2&nbsp;million for the Company&#146;s qualified and excess pension plans. In addition, at
December&nbsp;31, 2006, a gain of approximately $75,000, net of income tax, was recorded as a component
of other comprehensive income related to the Company&#146;s post-retirement benefits plan. Of the total
amounts recorded into accumulated other comprehensive income/(loss) as of December&nbsp;31, 2006, the
adoption of SFAS No.&nbsp;158 resulted in a loss of approximately $3.3&nbsp;million (after tax) associated
with the Company&#146;s pension plans, and the entire $75,000 gain (after tax) for the Company&#146;s
post-retirement benefit plan.
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->56<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Medicare Part D</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On December&nbsp;8, 2003, the Medicare Prescription Drug, Improvement and Modernization Act (the &#147;Act&#148;)
became law. The Act provides for a federal subsidy to sponsors of retiree health care benefit
plans that provide a prescription drug benefit that is at least actuarially equivalent to the
benefit established by the Act. On May&nbsp;19, 2004, the FASB issued Staff Position No.&nbsp;106-2,
&#147;Accounting and Disclosure Requirements Related to the Medicare Prescription Drug, Improvement and
Modernization Act of 2003&#148; (the &#147;FSP&#148;). The FSP provides guidance on accounting for the effects of
the Act, which resulted in a reduction in the accumulated projected benefit obligation for the
subsidy related to benefits attributed to past service. Treating the future subsidy under the Act
as an actuarial experience gain, as required by the guidance, decreased the accumulated projected
benefit obligation at the beginning of the third quarter of 2004 by approximately $0.6&nbsp;million.
The subsidy also decreased the net periodic post-retirement benefit cost for the last half of 2004
by less than $0.1&nbsp;million.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Measurement</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">For purposes of our consolidated financial statements, our plans&#146; measurement date is December&nbsp;31.
The market-related value of plan assets is determined based on the fair value at measurement date.
The projected benefit obligation is determined based on the present value of projected benefit
distributions at an assumed discount rate. The discount rate used reflects the rate at which we
believe the pension plan obligations could be effectively settled at the measurement date, as
though the pension benefits of all plan participants were determined as of that date.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Accumulated Benefit Obligation</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">An accumulated benefit obligation represents the actuarial present value of benefits. Whether
vested or non-vested, they are attributed by the pension benefit formula to employee services
rendered before a specified date using existing salary levels. As of December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005,
the accumulated benefit obligation for the Company&#146;s pension plans was $33.7&nbsp;million and $31.7&nbsp;million,
respectively. For the Company&#146;s post-retirement plan, our accumulated benefit obligation at December&nbsp;31,
2006 and 2005, was $9.8&nbsp;million and $9.5&nbsp;million, respectively.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Projected Benefit Obligation</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">A projected benefit obligation represents the actuarial present value as of a date of all benefits
attributed by the pension benefit formula to employee service performed before that date. It is
measured using assumptions as to future compensation levels, as the pension benefit formula is
based on those future salary levels.
</DIV>

funded status as of December&nbsp;31 for both years:
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Plan Assets</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company employs a total return approach whereby a mix of equities and fixed-income investments
are used to maximize the long-term return of plan assets for a prudent level of risk. Risk
tolerance is established through careful consideration of plan liabilities, plan funded status, and
corporate financial condition. The investment portfolio contains a diversified blend of equity and
fixed-income investments. Furthermore, equity investments are diversified across U.S. and non-U.S.
stocks, and include small and large capitalizations with an emphasis on large capitalization
stocks. Other assets, such as real estate, are used to enhance long-term returns while providing
additional portfolio diversification. Derivatives may be used to gain market exposure in an
efficient and timely manner; however, derivatives may not be used to leverage the portfolio beyond
the market value of the underlying investments. For the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005,
no derivatives were utilized. Investment risk is measured and monitored on an on-going basis
through quarterly investment portfolio reviews and annual liability measurements.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The expected long-term rate of return on plan assets is estimated based on the plan&#146;s actual
historical return results, the allowable allocation of plan assets by investment class, market
conditions and other relevant factors. The Company evaluates whether the actual allocation has fallen within
an allowable range, and then the Company evaluates actual asset returns in total and by asset class.
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->58<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Expected Contributions</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">During 2007, the Company expects to contribute approximately $153,000 to its excess pension plan.
The Company does not expect to make any contributions during 2007 to its qualified pension plan.
In addition, the Company expects to contribute approximately $552,000 during 2007, net of expected
Medicare Part&nbsp;D reimbursements, for benefit payments to its post-retirement benefit plan.

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Periodic Cost</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">As permitted under SFAS No.&nbsp;87, &#147;Employers&#146; Accounting for Pensions,&#148; the amortization of any prior
service cost is determined using a straight-line amortization of the cost over the average
remaining service period of employees expected to receive benefits under the pension and
post-retirement plans.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Other</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company has a 401(k)/profit sharing plan that covers all of its employees, including employees
of its subsidiaries. Amounts determinable under the plan are contributed in part to a profit
sharing trust qualified under the Internal Revenue Code with the remainder paid as cash bonuses,
equity awards and matching 401(k) employee contributions. During the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2006
and 2005, the Company made contributions of approximately $3.0&nbsp;million and $2.5&nbsp;million,
respectively, to the profit sharing trust for profit sharing awards and matching 401(k) employee
contributions.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company has a non-qualified deferred compensation program whereby certain key employees can
elect to defer receipt of all or a portion of their cash bonuses until a certain date or until
retirement, termination, death or disability. The deferred compensation liabilities incur interest
expense at the prime rate or at a rate of return of one of several managed funds sponsored by the
Company, as selected by the participant. The Company mitigates its exposure relating to
participants who have selected a fund return by investing in the underlying fund at the time of the
deferral. At December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005, the Company&#146;s deferred compensation liability was
approximately $41.6&nbsp;million and $36.6&nbsp;million, respectively.
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>9.&nbsp;&nbsp;STOCK-BASED COMPENSATION</B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company currently maintains two stock-based compensation plans, the Second Amended and Restated
Nuveen 1996 Equity Incentive Award Plan (the &#147;1996 Plan&#148;) and the 2005 Equity Incentive Plan (the
&#147;2005 Plan&#148;). Under the 1996 Plan, the Company had reserved an aggregate of 30,900,000 shares of
Class&nbsp;A common stock for awards. Under the 2005 Plan, the Company has reserved an aggregate of
7,000,000 shares of Class&nbsp;A common stock for awards. Under both plans, options may be awarded at
exercise prices not less than 100% of the fair market value of the stock on the grant date, and
maximum option terms may not exceed ten years.
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Restricted Stock</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">At the date of the grant, the recipient of restricted stock awards has all rights of a stockholder,
including voting and dividend rights, subject to certain restrictions on transferability and a risk
of forfeiture. Restricted stock grants typically vest over a period of either 3&nbsp;years or 6&nbsp;years
beginning on the date of grant.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In 2004, the Company granted 9,208 shares of restricted stock with a weighted-average fair value of
$25.86. In 2005, the Company granted 611,329 shares of restricted stock with a weighted-average
fair value of $38.01. In 2006, the Company granted 363,324 shares of restricted stock with a
weighted-average fair value of $43.12. The Company awarded 325,547 shares of restricted stock with
a weighted-average fair value of $51.54 in
</DIV>
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->62<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Stock Options</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company also awarded certain employees options to purchase the Company&#146;s common stock at
exercise prices equal to or greater than the closing market price of the stock on the day the
options were awarded. Options awarded pursuant to the 1996 Plan and the 2005 Plan are generally
subject to three- and four-year cliff vesting and expire ten years from the award date. The
Company awarded options to purchase 580,121 shares of common stock in February&nbsp;2007 to employees
pursuant to the Company&#146;s incentive compensation program for 2006. There were approximately
6,982,000 shares available for future equity awards as of December&nbsp;31, 2006, after consideration of
the February&nbsp;2007 incentive awards.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Effective April&nbsp;1, 2004, the Company began expensing the cost of stock options per the fair value
recognition provisions of SFAS No.&nbsp;123, &#147;Accounting for Stock-Based Compensation&#148; (see &#147;Equity
Incentive Plans&#148; in Note 1). The retroactive restatement method described in SFAS No.&nbsp;148,
&#147;Accounting for Stock-Based Compensation &#150; Transition and Disclosure&#148; was adopted and the results
for prior years have been restated. Compensation cost recognized is the same as that which would
have been recognized had the fair value method of SFAS No.&nbsp;123 been applied from its original
effective date. Prior to April&nbsp;1, 2004, the Company
accounted for stock option plans under the provisions of APB Opinion No.&nbsp;25, &#147;Accounting for Stock
Issued to Employees&#148; and related interpretations.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Effective January&nbsp;1, 2006 , the Company adopted SFAS No.&nbsp;123R, &#147;Share Based Payment.&#148; Because the
fair value recognition provisions of SFAS No.&nbsp;123, &#147;Stock-Based Compensation,&#148; and SFAS No.&nbsp;123R
were materially consistent under our equity plans, the adoption of SFAS No.&nbsp;123R did not have a
significant impact on our financial position or our results of operations. In accordance with SFAS
No.&nbsp;123R, stock option compensation expense of approximately $17.7&nbsp;million, $14.5&nbsp;million and $20.4
million has been recognized
</DIV>
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->63<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">for 2006, 2005 and 2004, respectively. Included in compensation
expense for 2006 is amortization related to a long-term equity performance plan discussed below.
Included in compensation expense for 2004 is approximately $4.3&nbsp;million of stock option
compensation expense recognized due to a change in the assumed vesting period for certain options
that had a vesting period that was accelerated based on stock performance. As of December&nbsp;31,
2006, there was approximately $20.0&nbsp;million of total unrecognized compensation costs related to
stock options. These costs are expected to be recognized over a weighted-average period of 3.2
years.
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Long-Term Equity Performance Plan</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In January&nbsp;2005, the Company granted long-term equity performance (&#147;LTEP&#148;) awards consisting of
269,300 restricted shares and 1,443,000 options to senior managers. These grants will be awarded
only if specified Company-wide performance criteria are met and are subject to additional
time-based vesting if the performance criteria are met. During the third quarter of 2006,
management determined that it appeared probable the Company will meet the performance requirements
as set forth in the LTEP plan. As a result, during the third quarter of 2006, the Company expensed
a total of $7.6&nbsp;million related to the LTEP awards, which included $4.2&nbsp;million of a &#147;catch-up&#148;
adjustment for amortization for prior periods from the date of the LTEP grant (January&nbsp;2005)
through January&nbsp;2006.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Share repurchases are utilized, among other things, to reduce the dilutive impact of our
stock-based plans. At December&nbsp;31, 2006, the Company had one approved share repurchase plan in
place with 6.6&nbsp;million shares remaining to be purchased. Repurchased shares are converted to
Treasury shares and are used to satisfy stock option exercises, as needed. Share repurchase
activity is dependent, among other things, on the availability of excess cash after meeting
business and capital requirements. Therefore, the timing and amount of repurchases is not known
and we do not have an estimate of the number of shares expected to be repurchased during 2007.
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>10.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ACQUISITION OF NWQ INVESTMENT MANAGEMENT COMPANY, INC.</B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On August&nbsp;1, 2002, Nuveen Investments completed the acquisition of NWQ Investment Management
Company, Inc. (&#147;NWQ&#148;). NWQ specializes in value-oriented equity investments and has significant
relationships with institutions and financial advisors serving high-net-worth investors. The
acquisition price includes potential additional future payments up to a maximum of $20.5&nbsp;million
over a five year period that can be offset by fees paid to seller affiliates under a strategic
alliance agreement. As these future payments relate to a take-or-pay type of contract, the $20.5
million was recorded as both goodwill and a corresponding
liability on the Company&#146;s consolidated balance sheet. During 2006 and 2005, $4.9&nbsp;million and $3.9
million, respectively, were paid against this $20.5&nbsp;million liability. As of December&nbsp;31, 2006 and
2005, the remaining liability of $6.1&nbsp;million and $11.0&nbsp;million, respectively, is included as $6.1
million in other short-term liabilities on the accompanying consolidated balance sheet as of
December&nbsp;31, 2006 and $4.9&nbsp;million in other short-term liabilities and $6.1&nbsp;million in other
long-term liabilities on the accompanying consolidated balance sheet as of December&nbsp;31, 2005.
(Refer also to Note 6, &#147;Equity Programs.&#148;)
</DIV>


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->65<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>11.&nbsp;&nbsp;SANTA BARBARA ASSET MANAGEMENT ACQUISITION</B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On October&nbsp;3, 2005, the Company completed the acquisition of Santa Barbara Asset Management (&#147;Santa
Barbara&#148;), an investment manager with approximately $3&nbsp;billion of assets under management at the
time of the acquisition. Santa Barbara specializes in managing growth stock portfolios for
institutions and high-net-worth investors. As a result of the acquisition, Nuveen Investments has
further diversified its asset base. The Company paid approximately $50&nbsp;million of cash
consideration for Santa Barbara. The results of Santa Barbara operations are included in our
consolidated statements of income since the acquisition date.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Of the total purchase price, approximately $0.7&nbsp;million has been allocated to the net book value of
assets acquired. Net book value consisted primarily of fee receivables and payables. The purchase
price plus the net book value of assets acquired were allocated to identifiable intangible assets
and goodwill.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company engaged external valuation experts to determine the appropriate purchase price
allocation for the Santa Barbara acquisition. The purchase price allocation valuation indicates
that approximately $27.9&nbsp;million of the purchase price in excess of the net book value of assets
acquired is assignable to intangible assets, of which $26.2&nbsp;million relates to customer
relationships (9&nbsp;year useful life) and $1.7&nbsp;million to the Santa Barbara Trademark / Tradename (9
year useful life).
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">There were no unamortizable intangible assets acquired in the Santa Barbara acquisition. For the
years ended December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005, amortization expense for Santa Barbara intangibles was $3.5
million and $0.4&nbsp;million, respectively. The estimated amortization expense for each of the next
five years is $2.9&nbsp;million for the Santa Barbara customer relationships intangible asset, and $0.2
million for the Santa Barbara Trademark/Tradename intangible asset. In addition, the Company
expects to be able to deduct, for tax purposes, approximately $2.6&nbsp;million for each of the next
five years for goodwill amortization.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Refer also to Note 6, &#147;Equity Programs.&#148;
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>12.&nbsp;&nbsp;CONSOLIDATED FUNDS</B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">During 2004, the Company created and invested in six new funds, all managed by two of the Company&#146;s
subsidiaries. During 2005, three of the six funds were marketed to the public and the Company&#146;s
investment in those three funds was reduced to a non-controlling minority position. At December
31, 2005, the Company was the sole investor in only three of the original six funds. During 2006,
although the remaining three funds in which the Company was the sole investor at December&nbsp;31, 2005
were marketed to the public, at December&nbsp;31, 2006, the Company held a majority investment position
in these three funds. The investment strategy for these three remaining funds is taxable
fixed-income with various objectives: short-duration, multi-strategy core and high yield. The
Company&#146;s total investment in these three funds is $30.0&nbsp;million.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Under the provisions of Accounting Research Bulletin No.&nbsp;51, &#147;Consolidated Financial Statements,&#148;
as amended by SFAS No.&nbsp;94, &#147;Consolidation of All Majority-Owned Subsidiaries,&#148; the Company is
required to consolidate into its financial results those funds in which the Company is either the
sole investor or in which the Company holds a majority investment position. Due to the requirement
to consolidate, the assets and liabilities of the three funds discussed above are included
throughout the Company&#146;s December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005 consolidated balance sheets. In addition, the
income and expenses of these three funds is included in the Company&#146;s consolidated income
statements for the three years ended December&nbsp;31, 2006.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">At December&nbsp;31, 2006, the total assets of these three funds were approximately $54.1&nbsp;million and
total liabilities were approximately $16.8&nbsp;million. The net income for 2006 for these three funds
was approximately $1.8&nbsp;million and has been included in the Company&#146;s consolidated financial
results for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2006. At December&nbsp;31, 2005, the total assets of these
three funds were approximately $31.6&nbsp;million and total liabilities were approximately $2.6&nbsp;million.
The net income for 2005 for these three funds
</DIV>
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->66<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">was approximately $0.7&nbsp;million and has been included in the Company&#146;s consolidated financial
results for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2005.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Included in the total assets of these three funds are underlying securities in which the funds are
invested. At December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005, these underlying securities approximated $35.2&nbsp;million
and $28.3&nbsp;million, respectively. Although these underlying fund investments would be classified as
&#147;trading&#148; securities by the funds if the funds were to follow SFAS No.&nbsp;115, &#147;Accounting for Certain
Investments in Debt and Equity Securities,&#148; the Company does not classify the underlying fund
investments as &#147;trading&#148; securities, as the Company&#146;s objective for holding an investment in the
three funds is not to buy or sell frequently nor is it to generate profits. The Company&#146;s
objective is to hold the fund investments until such time that they are majority-owned by outside
investors.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">A new share repurchase program was publicly announced and approved on August&nbsp;9, 2006. This program

previous authorization, the Company is authorized to repurchase up to 7.4&nbsp;million shares of common
stock. As of December&nbsp;31, 2006, the remaining authorization covered approximately 6.6&nbsp;million
shares. There is not a pre-determined expiration date for this plan.

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>14.&nbsp;&nbsp;NET CAPITAL REQUIREMENT</B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Nuveen Investments, LLC, the Company&#146;s wholly-owned broker-dealer subsidiary, is a Delaware limited
liability company and is subject to the Securities and Exchange Commission Rule&nbsp;15c3-1, the
&#147;Uniform Net Capital Rule,&#148; which requires the maintenance of minimum net capital and requires that
the ratio of aggregate indebtedness to net capital, as these terms are defined, shall not exceed 15
to 1. At December&nbsp;31, 2006, our broker-dealer&#146;s net capital ratio was 5.33 to 1 and its net
capital was approximately $8.1&nbsp;million, which is $5.2&nbsp;million in excess of the required net capital
of $2.9&nbsp;million.
</DIV>


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->67<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD align="right">33.230</TD>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD align="right">37.240</TD>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>

    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
</TR>
<!-- End Table Body -->
</TABLE>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Nuveen Investments, Inc. common stock is listed on the New York Stock Exchange under the symbol
&#147;JNC.&#148; There are no contractual restrictions on the Company&#146;s present ability to pay dividends on
its common stock.
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>16.&nbsp;&nbsp;GAIN CONTINGENCY</B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">During the second quarter of 2006, the Company sold its minority investment in Institutional
Capital Corporation (&#147;ICAP&#148;), an institutional money manager which was acquired by New York Life
Investment Management. The Company recorded a $3.1&nbsp;million gain during the second quarter of 2006
as a result of the initial closing of this sale. During the third quarter of 2006, the Company
recorded a $5.8&nbsp;million gain related to cash payments received
related to this sale, based upon the partial satisfaction
of a contingency clause on investor approvals and client retention. During the fourth quarter of
2006, the Company recorded an additional $1.2&nbsp;million gain related to
cash payments received upon
investor approvals and the full satisfaction of client retention targets.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">If certain indemnification obligations are satisfied during 2007, the Company may potentially
receive an additional $5&nbsp;million during the fourth quarter of 2007 upon the release of funds from
an escrow established to cover any breaches of representations and warranties.
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>17.&nbsp;&nbsp;SUBSEQUENT EVENT</B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On February&nbsp;15, 2007, the Company exercised its right to call 25% of the Class&nbsp;4 NWQ minority
members&#146; interests for $22.6&nbsp;million. See Note 6, &#147;Equity Programs.&#148; Of the total amount to be
paid on March&nbsp;2, 2007, approximately $22.5&nbsp;million will be recorded as goodwill.
</DIV>

</DIV>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<DIV align="center" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 18pt"><B>Management&#146;s Report on Internal Control Over<BR>
Financial Reporting</B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Management of Nuveen Investments, Inc., together with its consolidated subsidiaries (the
&#147;Company&#148;), is responsible for establishing and maintaining adequate internal control over
financial reporting. The Company&#146;s internal control over financial reporting is a process designed
under the supervision of the Company&#146;s executive and financial officers to provide reasonable
assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporting and the preparation of the Company&#146;s
financial statements for external reporting purposes in accordance with accounting principles
generally accepted in the United States of America.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">As of December&nbsp;31, 2006, management conducted an assessment of the effectiveness of the Company&#146;s
internal control over financial reporting based on the framework established in <I>Internal Control &#151;
Integrated Framework </I>issued by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission
(&#147;COSO&#148;). Based on this assessment, management has determined that the Company&#146;s internal control
over financial reporting as of December&nbsp;31, 2006, is effective.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Our internal control over financial reporting includes policies and procedures that pertain to the
maintenance of records that, in reasonable detail, accurately and fairly reflect transactions and
dispositions of assets; provide reasonable assurance that transactions are recorded as necessary
to permit the preparation of financial statements in accordance with accounting principles generally
accepted in the United States of America, and that receipts and expenditures are being made only in
accordance with authorizations of management and the directors of the Company; and provide
reasonable assurance regarding prevention or timely detection of unauthorized acquisition, use or
disposition of the Company&#146;s assets that could have a material effect on our financial statements.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Management&#146;s assessment of the effectiveness of the Company&#146;s internal control over financial
reporting as of December&nbsp;31, 2006, has been audited by KPMG LLP, an independent registered public
accounting firm, as stated in their report appearing on pages 71 and 72 which expresses unqualified
opinions on management&#146;s assessment and on the effectiveness of the Company&#146;s internal control over
financial reporting as of December&nbsp;31, 2006.
</DIV>


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->70<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

subsidiaries (the Company) as of December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005, and the related consolidated
statements of income, changes in common stockholders&#146; equity, and cash flows for each of the years
in the three-year period ended December&nbsp;31, 2006. These consolidated financial statements are the
responsibility of the Company&#146;s management. Our responsibility is to express an opinion on these
consolidated financial statements based on our audits.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">We conducted our audits in accordance with the standards of the Public Company Accounting Oversight
Board (United States). Those standards require that we plan and perform the audit to obtain
reasonable assurance about whether the financial statements are free of material misstatement. An
audit includes examining, on a test basis, evidence supporting the amounts and disclosures in the
financial statements. An audit also includes assessing the accounting principles used and
significant estimates made by management, as well as evaluating the overall financial statement
presentation. We believe that our audits provide a reasonable basis for our opinion.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In our opinion, the consolidated financial statements referred to above present fairly, in all
material respects, the financial position of the Company as of December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005, and the
results of their operations and their cash flows for each of the years in the three-year period
ended December&nbsp;31, 2006, in conformity with U.S. generally accepted accounting principles.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">We also have audited, in accordance with the standards of the Public Company Accounting Oversight
Board (United States), the effectiveness of the Company&#146;s internal control over financial reporting
as of December&nbsp;31, 2006, based on criteria established in Internal Control&#151;Integrated Framework
issued by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission (COSO), and our
report dated February&nbsp;26, 2007 expressed an unqualified opinion on management&#146;s assessment of, and
the effective operation of, internal control over financial reporting.
</DIV>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<DIV align="center" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 18pt"><U>Report of Independent Registered Public Accounting Firm</U>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Board of Directors and Stockholders<BR>
Nuveen Investments, Inc.:

</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">We have audited management&#146;s assessment, included in the accompanying Management&#146;s Report on
Internal Control over Financial Reporting, that Nuveen Investments, Inc. (the Company) maintained
effective internal control over financial reporting as of December&nbsp;31, 2006, based on criteria
established in Internal Control&#151;Integrated Framework issued by the Committee of Sponsoring
Organizations of the Treadway Commission (COSO). The Company&#146;s management is responsible for
maintaining effective internal control over financial reporting and for its assessment of the
effectiveness of internal control over financial reporting. Our responsibility is to express an
opinion on management&#146;s assessment and an opinion on the effectiveness of the Company&#146;s internal
control over financial reporting based on our audit.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">We conducted our audit in accordance with the standards of the Public Company Accounting Oversight
Board (United States). Those standards require that we plan and perform the audit to obtain
reasonable assurance about whether effective internal control over financial reporting was
maintained in all material respects. Our audit included obtaining an understanding of internal
control over financial reporting, evaluating management&#146;s assessment, testing and evaluating the
design and operating effectiveness of internal control, and performing such other procedures as we
considered necessary in the circumstances. We believe that our audit provides a reasonable basis
for our opinion.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">A company&#146;s internal control over financial reporting is a process designed to provide reasonable
assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporting and the preparation of financial
statements for external purposes in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles. A
company&#146;s internal control over financial reporting includes those policies and procedures that (1)
pertain to the maintenance of records that, in reasonable detail, accurately and fairly reflect the
transactions and dispositions of the assets of the company; (2)&nbsp;provide reasonable assurance that
transactions are recorded as necessary to permit preparation of financial statements in accordance
with generally accepted accounting principles, and that receipts and expenditures of the company
are being made only in accordance with authorizations of management and directors of the company;
and (3)&nbsp;provide reasonable assurance regarding prevention or timely detection of unauthorized
acquisition, use, or disposition of the company&#146;s assets that could have a material effect on the
financial statements.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Because of its inherent limitations, internal control over financial reporting may not prevent or
detect misstatements. Also, projections of any evaluation of effectiveness to future periods are
subject to the risk that controls may become inadequate because of changes in conditions, or that
the degree of compliance with the policies or procedures may deteriorate.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In our opinion, management&#146;s assessment that the Company maintained effective internal control over
financial reporting as of December&nbsp;31, 2006, is fairly stated, in all material respects, based on
criteria established in Internal Control&#151;Integrated Framework issued by the Committee of Sponsoring
Organizations of the Treadway Commission (COSO). Also, in our opinion, the Company maintained, in
all material respects, effective internal control over financial reporting as of December&nbsp;31, 2006,
based on criteria established in Internal Control&#151;Integrated Framework issued by the Committee of
Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission (COSO).
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">We also have audited, in accordance with the standards of the Public Company Accounting Oversight
Board (United States), the consolidated balance sheets of the Company as of December&nbsp;31, 2006 and
2005, and the related consolidated statements of operations, changes in common stockholders&#146;
equity, and cash flows for each of the years in the three-year period ended December&nbsp;31, 2006, and
our report dated February&nbsp;26, 2007 expressed an unqualified opinion on those consolidated financial
statements.
</DIV>

LLP
